href="/search/108081209214649/places-in/197871390225897/places/intersect/">See all Cafe in Las Vegas</a></div><div><div class="clearfix"><div class="_3vdi _3-95 lfloat _ohe"><div class="clearfix _1sj2"><a class="_8o lfloat _ohe" href="https://www.facebook.com/pages/Paradise-Nevada/107894812567127" tabindex="-1" aria-hidden="true"><img class="_s0 _4ooo _1sj6 img" src="https://external-frt3-2.xx.fbcdn.net/safe_image.php?d=AQB69fDZV9CdzJQj&amp;w=158&amp;h=158&amp;url=https%3A%2F%2Fupload.wikimedia.org%2Fwikipedia%2Fcommons%2Fthumb%2F2%2F2b%2FLas_Vegas%252C_Planet_Hollywood.jpg%2F720px-Las_Vegas%252C_Planet_Hollywood.jpg&amp;cfs=1&amp;fallback=hub_likes&amp;f&amp;_nc_hash=AQCtiGGX--EC4y_e" alt="" aria-label="Paradise, Nevada" role="img" style="width:158px;height:158px" /></a><div class="_42ef"><div class="_1sj3 _3-8j"><div class="_1sj4"><div class="_1sj9"><a class="_1sja" href="https://www.facebook.com/pages/Paradise-Nevada/107894812567127"><div class="ellipsis" id="u_0_2u" data-hover="tooltip">Paradise, Nevada</div></a><span class="_1jn2">4.2 <span class="_1jn3">★</span></span></div><a class="_39g6" href="https://www.facebook.com/pages/Paradise-Nevada/107894812567127?sk=info"><p class="_1sj5 _3-8w">Paradise is an unincorporated town and census-designated place (CDP) in Clark County, Nevada, United States, adjacent to the city of Las Vegas. The population was 223,167 at the 2010 census, making it the most populous unincorporated community in Nevada and more populous than any city in the state outside Clark County. As an unincorporated town, it is governed by the Clark County Commission with input from the Paradise Town Advisory Board. Paradise was formed on December 8, 1950.Paradise contains McCarran International Airport; the University of Nevada, Las Vegas; and most of the Las Vegas Strip. Paradise contains most tourist attractions in the Las Vegas area, excluding downtown. Despite this, the name Paradise remains relatively unknown. All Paradise ZIP codes have Las Vegas mailing addresses.HistoryThe southern part of the Las Vegas Valley was referred to as Paradise Valley as early as 1910, owing to a high water table that made the land particularly fertile for farming. County commissioners established a Paradise school district in 1914.In 1950, mayor Ernie Cragin of Las Vegas, looking to fund an ambitious building agenda and pay down the city's rising debt, sought to expand the city's tax base by annexing the Las Vegas Strip which was unincorporated territory. A group of casino executives, led by Gus Greenbaum of the Flamingo, lobbied the county commissioners for township status which would prevent the city from annexing the land without the commission's approval. The commission voted to create the unincorporated township of Paradise on December 8, 1950.</p></a></div><div class="_1sj7"><div class="_1sj8"><div class="clearfix"><div class="_3-90 lfloat _ohe"><i class="_1sjd"></div><div><div class="_1sje"><span class="_1sjf"><strong>What people say</strong></span><a href="/candy.mendell/activity/10212420033047311"><p class="_1sj5 _1sjb _3-8x">Polynesian restaurant/bars are very near and dear to our hearts. We had our first date at one back home in California almost 38 years ago and ended up having our wedding rehearsal dinner there! When we moved to Henderson last year, we were so excited Vegas had a couple for us to try and last night was our first time checking out The Golden Tiki. We thoroughly enjoyed the cocktails, especially the Mai Tai's! The décor, music and snippets of old 60's beachy, surfin', sci-fi, Hawaiian themed movies and such on the television behind the bar, really set the mood. We totally felt like we were on vacation! I would have given 5 stars, but we were under the impression they served food. We came in hungry for appetizers, only to find out they only serve food on Friday and Saturday nights and it's very limited. When it's gone, it's gone! So before we sat down for cocktails, we had to go find food a few doors down. Luckily there are plenty of places to eat nearby, but nothing compares to a Polynesian Pupu Platter to accompany your Mai Tai's. We will definitely be back, with or without food. We are unable to come in on the weekends, so I guess sadly it will be without.</p></a><div class="clearfix"><img class="_s0 _4ooo _8o _8r lfloat _ohe _ry img" We arrived yesterday after a very long day of delayed then cancelled, then more delayed flights and airport headaches. We were tired, hungry, and weren't feeling excited any more, just wanted to crash and forget the whole flight experience we had with allegiant. We showed up looking as bad as we felt. We were greeted with smiles, shared our troubles, and everyone made us feel right at home and gave us the energy boost we needed to get excited for Vegas again! They upgraded our room to a better view with better wireless reception, even took us into the diamond club check in to bypass the wait and give us time to get checked in and decompress. The shops and restaurants are perfect, not the typical Vegas hotel shops that no one will ever shop in. Walk right out the side door to the Linq promenade and enjoy a delicious variety of restaurants, cupcakes, and of course, great drink specials! Our rooms were very clean, comfy, and huge! We are staying in the Fab deluxe, which is one of their cheaper rooms, and it is worth way more than the price! Comfy beds, lots of amenities already in room, great pool and gym, super walkable hotel and casino area (no getting lost or having to backtrack constantly). We are here all week and I am so relieved AND excited that we are spending it here at the Flamingo! I can't think of one reason to not stay here, we are lifetime flamingos guests for sure!! href="/search/108081209214649/places-in/935165616516865/places/intersect/">See all Outdoors in Las Vegas</a></div><div><div class="clearfix"><div class="_3vdi _3-95 lfloat _ohe"><div class="clearfix _1sj2"><a class="_8o lfloat _ohe" href="https://www.facebook.com/pages/Floyd-Lamb-Park-at-Tule-Springs/112903198721121" tabindex="-1" aria-hidden="true"><img class="_s0 _4ooo _1sj6 img" src="https://external-frt3-2.xx.fbcdn.net/safe_image.php?d=AQA92ZHbQgpMPt6P&amp;w=158&amp;h=158&amp;url=http%3A%2F%2Fupload.wikimedia.org%2Fwikipedia%2Fen%2Fthumb%2F2%2F2a%2FTuleSpringsLake.jpg%2F720px-TuleSpringsLake.jpg&amp;cfs=1&amp;fallback=hub_likes&amp;f&amp;_nc_hash=AQDXXgoPeaBP6LPm" alt="" aria-label="Floyd Lamb Park at Tule Springs" role="img" style="width:158px;height:158px" /></a><div class="_42ef"><div class="_1sj3 _3-8j"><div class="_1sj4"><div class="_1sj9"><a class="_1sja" href="https://www.facebook.com/pages/Floyd-Lamb-Park-at-Tule-Springs/112903198721121"><div class="ellipsis" id="u_0_39" data-hover="tooltip">Floyd Lamb Park at Tule Springs</div></a><span class="_1jn2">4.4 <span class="_1jn3">★</span></span></div><a class="_39g6" href="https://www.facebook.com/pages/Floyd-Lamb-Park-at-Tule-Springs/112903198721121?sk=info"><p class="_1sj5 _3-8w">Floyd Lamb Park at Tule Springs is a 2040acre park in Las Vegas, Nevada. The park is centered on Tule Springs, a series of small lakes that formed an oasis in this part of the Mojave Desert. One of the larger urban retreats in the Las Vegas Valley, Tule Springs was once considered to be far out of town but is now encroached by development. The park includes the Tule Springs Ranch, Tule Springs Archaeological Site, Tule Springs Wash and four ponds available for fishing.HistoryThe springs was first designated as a park when it was acquired by the city of Las Vegas in 1964. It was renamed Floyd Lamb State Park in 1977 when the state assumed control. The park was named after Nevada state senator Floyd Lamb, who was later convicted of taking a $23,000 bribe from an undercover FBI agent in 1983.The city took control of the park for a second time when the legislature and state in 2005 agreed to release control and ownership of Floyd Lamb State Park to the City of Las Vegas. The park was transferred to the city, on July 2, 2007 and renamed to Floyd Lamb Park at Tule Springs. In addition to the park, the city received control of 1300acre of Bureau of Land Management land.</p></a></div><div class="_1sj7"><div class="_1sj8"><div class="clearfix"><div class="_3-90 lfloat
